     <p>The College of Arts and Sciences (CAS) was formerly named the College of Liberal Arts (CLA). The College of Communication was formerly named the School of Public Communication (SPC). The School of Management (SMG) was formerly named the College of Business Administration (CBA). The College of General Studies (CGS) was formerly named the College of Basic Studies (CBS). The School of Nursing (SON) and the College of Practical Arts and Letters (PAL) are units that have been discontinued.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The Department of Cognitive and Neural Systems' technology lab, directed by <a href="/wiki/Gail_Carpenter" title="Gail Carpenter">Gail Carpenter</a> has software, on topics ranging from remote sensing to text mining, available for download.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

     <p><i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranks Boston University 51 among national universities for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Boston University was also ranked 11th among public health graduate schools, 22nd among law schools, 22nd among social work schools, 31st among business schools, 34th among medical schools, 42nd among engineering schools, and 56th among education schools.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, Emerging, a human resources company based in Paris, and Trendence, an institute that researches employer branding, personal marketing and recruitment, ranked Boston University 17th worldwide and 7th in the United States for employability of its graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> in 2012 ranked Boston University 64th overall in the world, the 23rd highest ranked U.S. school on its list. It has also received the maximum five stars under the QS Stars evaluation system.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> in 2011 ranked Boston University 54th overall in the world, the 32nd highest ranked U.S. school on its list.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a>'</i>s <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> ranks Boston University 43rd in the United States, and 71st in the world, in its 2012 list of the Top 500 Universities.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> (International Edition), in its list of the Top 100 Global Universities, ranked Boston University the 35th in the United States, and 65th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In a 2003 survey, <a href="/wiki/Gallup_poll" title="Gallup poll" class="mw-redirect">Gallup polls</a> asked American adults, &quot;All in all, what would you say is the best college or university in the United States?&quot; Boston University was one of only 35 schools to be named by at least 1% of the American public as the best school in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Economics Department at Boston University is ranked 13th in the World by total citations as of May 2013. The ranking is based on 6133 institutions with 36221 registered authors in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank_of_St._Louis" title="Federal Reserve Bank of St. Louis">Federal Reserve Bank of St. Louis</a> database of economic papers.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, U.S. News &amp; World Report ranks Boston University 20th in the United States for economics and econometrics programs.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Biomedical Engineering Graduate and Undergraduate Programs are ranked 7th and 8th respectively in the nation and rising by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>. The undergraduate program is also the sixth-largest ABET-accredited program in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additionally, all of the professional graduate programs in the <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_College_of_Health_and_Rehabilitation_Sciences:_Sargent_College" title="Boston University College of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences: Sargent College" class="mw-redirect">Boston University College of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences: Sargent College</a> rank within the top 8% in the country. The Occupational Therapy Program ranked 2nd out of 156 programs; the Physical Therapy Program ranked 16th out of 201 programs; and the Speech-Language Pathology Program ranked 21st out of 250 programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Sargent_College_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sargent_College-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Business_Week" title="Business Week" class="mw-redirect">Business Week</a></i> ranks Boston University's MBA program 38th, and its undergraduate business program 18th.<sup id="cite_ref-BWUGrad_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWUGrad-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>The Economist</i> ranks <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_University_School_of_Management" title="Boston University School of Management">Boston University School of Management</a></i> 42nd among global MBA programs in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Financial_Times" title="The Financial Times" class="mw-redirect">The Financial Times</a></i> ranks Boston University's MBA program 68th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FTMba_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTMba-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Quantnet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Quantnet (page does not exist)">Quantnet</a></i> ranks Boston University's Mathematical Finance program 17th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-QNFinmath_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QNFinmath-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG/250px-Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG/375px-Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG/500px-Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Boston_University_Talbot_Building_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Talbot Building located on the medical campus houses the 
        <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_School_of_Public_Health" title="Boston University School of Public Health">School of Public Health</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="The Center for Measuring University Performance" class="mw-redirect">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> ranks Boston University among the top 50 research universities in the country</p> 
     <p>BU is one of 96 American universities receiving the highest research classification (&quot;RU/VH&quot;) by the Carnegie Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_Foundation_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie_Foundation-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2010, the University Ranking by Academic Performance (URAP) conducted by the Informatics Institute of <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Technical_University" title="Middle East Technical University">Middle East Technical University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> ranked Boston University 64th in the world and 33rd in the United States. The criteria for the URAP was an aggregation of six academic research performance indicators: current productivity (number of published articles), long-term productivity (from <a href="/wiki/Google_Scholar" title="Google Scholar">Google Scholar</a>), research impact (citations from <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Scientific_Information" title="Institute for Scientific Information">Institute for Scientific Information</a>), impact (cumulative journal impact), quality (H-index), and international collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 2011 Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities, produced by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT),<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> which is designed to assess research universities by measuring both long-term and short-term research performance, Boston University is ranked 54th in the World and 36th in the United States.</p> 
     <p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a> ranked Boston University among the top 53 American research universities overall, and among the top 33 private American research universities. Their methodology is based on data such as research publications, citations, recognitions and funding, as well as undergraduate quality such as SAT scores.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 2012 SCImago Institutions Rankings (SIR),<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> an international ranking of worldwide research institutions, ranked Boston University 129th in the world and 47th in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> SCImago Research Group,<sup id="cite_ref-sci_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sci-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> a Spain-based research organization, ranked schools in areas such as: research output, international collaboration, normalized impact and publication rate.<sup id="cite_ref-sci_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sci-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The 2013-14 school year full-time tuition totaled $43,970 with exceptions to some schools. The total cost including room and board averages $58,530.</p> 
     <p>On-campus dormitory housing ranges from $8,930 to $11,990 a year while more premium choices in the newer Student Village residence halls and on-campus apartments range from $11,210 to $15,990 a year. By comparison, the average rent for a two-bedroom apartment in the <a href="/wiki/Allston-Brighton" title="Allston-Brighton" class="mw-redirect">Allston-Brighton</a> area is $1,300, or $7,800 per person per year.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grade_deflation">Grade deflation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Grade deflation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The independently run student newspaper at Boston University, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Free_Press" title="The Daily Free Press">The Daily Free Press</a></i>, as well as <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDeflation_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTDeflation-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> have published articles exploring the existence of grade deflation. <i>The Times</i> discovered that administrators have suggested to faculty members deflated ideal grade distributions. Though an article in the staff's <i>BU Today</i> asserted that &quot;the GPAs of BU undergrads and the percentage of As and Bs have both risen over the last two decades&quot;, <i>The New York Times</i> has found BU grades rising more slowly with respect to many other schools.</p> 
     <p>In 2004, the average GPA of a BU undergraduate was 3.04,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> compared to the averages of 3.35 for Boston College, (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> 3.48 for Amherst College, (2006)<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> 3.41 for New York University (2002)<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> and 3.43 for Harvard University (2004).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>About 81 percent of all grades earned in either the A or B range (75% in the B range). The article went on to note that although the university attempted to curb <a href="/wiki/Grade_inflation" title="Grade inflation">grade inflation</a> and inconsistency in the late 1990s both the percentage of A's and GPAs have been rising since. They attributed the grade deflation not to teachers' grading policies, but to the increasing quality of each incoming class which leads to more top grades.<sup id="cite_ref-BUTodayGradeDeflation_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUTodayGradeDeflation-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Journals_and_publications">Journals and publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Journals and publications">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Boston University is home to several academic journals and publications. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_School_of_Law" title="Boston University School of Law">School of Law</a> hosts six nationally recognized law journals, including the <i>Boston University Law Review</i>, <i>American Journal of Law and Medicine</i>, <i>Review of Banking &amp; Financial Law</i>, <i>Boston University International Law Journal</i>, <i>Journal of Science and Technology Law</i>, and <i>Public Interest Law Journal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_School_of_Education" title="Boston University School of Education">School of Education</a> houses <i>The Journal of Education</i>, which is the oldest continuously published journal in the field of education in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Boston University College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a>, <i>Studies in Romanticism</i> is housed at the Department of English<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>The Journal of Field Archeology</i> is housed at the Department of Archeology.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The Department of History is affiliated with The Historical Society, which publishes <i>The Journal of the Historical Society</i> and <i>Historically Speaking</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Society_Web_Site_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Society_Web_Site-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>American Journal of Media Psychology</i> and the <i>Public Relations Journal</i> are currently edited by professors at the <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_College_of_Communication" title="Boston University College of Communication">College of Communication</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> which is also home to the <i>New England Center for Investigative Reporting</i>, which generates numerous publications yearly.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also offers its undergraduates the opportunity to publish exceptional work in <i>WR: Journal of the CAS Writing Program</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WR:_Journal_of_the_CAS_Writing_Program_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WR:_Journal_of_the_CAS_Writing_Program-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_academic_programs">Special academic programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Special academic programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Core_Curriculum">Core Curriculum</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Core Curriculum">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:326px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BU_CAS_(night).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg/324px-BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg" width="324" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg/486px-BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg/648px-BU_CAS_%28night%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BU_CAS_(night).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_gothic" title="Collegiate gothic" class="mw-redirect">collegiate gothic</a> towers of the School of Theology and the College of Arts and Sciences in the center of campus at night.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Offered in the College of Arts and Sciences, the Core Curriculum offers an intensive <a href="/wiki/Great_books" title="Great books">great books</a> program for any incoming freshmen who choose to participate. Occupying two classes a semester during freshman and sophomore years, the program has four humanities sections which start with the <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">Epic of Gilgamesh</a> and work their way through <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aeschylus" title="Aeschylus">Aeschylus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machiavelli" title="Machiavelli" class="mw-redirect">Machiavelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" title="Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect">Shakespeare</a>, Milton, Dante, Bach and many more. The Social Sciences part of the program includes Hobbes, <a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a>, Rousseau, Adam Smith, Marx, and continues through contemporary works. Lastly, the science aspect of the program deals with major ideas such as big bang theory, evolution, quantum mechanics and more. Ultimately, the program seeks to combine science, math, humanities, art, and the social sciences into a cohesive program to give students insight into their world and help them become more refined writers and scholars.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="University_Professors_Program">University Professors Program</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: University Professors Program">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Professors_Program" title="University Professors Program">University Professors Program</a> (UNI) was an interdisciplinary program that allowed students to pursue a broad range of academic interests. With a student to faculty ratio of 4:1, UNI offered students a broad education in a more personalized atmosphere. Students took a common, intimate, &quot;Core&quot; program consisting of liberal arts courses taught by University Professors in small seminar settings. They then worked closely with an advisor to craft a course of study which led them to an interdisciplinary degree, culminating in a senior thesis. Based upon the report of an academic review committee, a new University-wide honors program was developed and the UNI program was replaced by the University Honors College.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kilachand_Honors_College">Kilachand Honors College</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Kilachand Honors College">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The University Honors College matriculated its first class in 2010. In 2011, it was renamed Arvind and Chandan Nandlal Kilachand Honors College following a $25M donation from Rajen Kilachand; the largest donation in the history of the University. The Kilachand Honors College is a university-wide community of faculty and students dedicated to preserving, renewing, and rethinking classic ideals of liberal education: love of learning, intellectual curiosity, self-discovery, empathy, clarity of thought and expression. It rests on three pillars: an integrated, four-year curriculum; an extensive series of co-curricular events that include site-visits to leading cultural institutions as well as talks and readings by leading figures in the arts, sciences, and professions; and, finally, a “living and learning” community that offers students the personal atmosphere of a small liberal arts college and fosters responsibility and citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boston_University_Academy">Boston University Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Boston University Academy">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_Academy" title="Boston University Academy">Boston University Academy</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Boston University Academy is a private high school operated by Boston University. Founded in 1993, the school sits within the university's campus and students are offered the opportunity to take university courses.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_publications">Student publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student publications">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Despite a Student Activities policy which prohibits student-run publications from receiving University funding for printing costs, student journals continue to thrive at Boston University as department-sponsored publications, edited by students under the supervision of faculty and staff advisors. The coordinator for undergraduate publications, responsible for acquainting new editors with University guidelines and directing publications staff to campus production and financial resources, has been Zachary Bos of the Core Curriculum since 2006.</p> 
     <p>Although officially and entirely independent from the University, <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Free_Press" title="Daily Free Press" class="mw-redirect">The Daily Free Press</a></i> (often referred to as <i>The FreeP</i>), is the campus student newspaper, and the fourth largest daily newspaper in Boston. Since 1970, it has provided students with campus news, city and state news, sports coverage, editorials, arts and entertainment, and special feature stories. <i>The Daily Free Press</i> is published every regular instruction day of the University year and is available at BU dorms, classroom buildings and commercial locations frequented by students.</p> 
     <p><i>Synapse</i> is the Boston University Undergraduate Science Magazine and is published online every semester. The &quot;Science&quot; focus is on many disciplines ranging from life sciences to physical sciences, engineering to mathematics, and finance to economics. The magazine is peer and faculty reviewed, and is advertised with routine, campus-wide distribution of pamphlets highlighting featured articles. <i>Synapse</i> was first published in the spring of 2009 and continues to publish articles each semester.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>The Brownstone Journal</i> is the longest-running campus publication, having been publishing undergraduate research, scholarly articles and essays, and literary work in translation, since 1982. The Brownstone is currently sponsored by the Undergraduate Research Opportunities Program, but was originally a departmental publication of the University Professors Program. The staff operates from their offices in the former yearbook space in the basement of 10 Lenox Street, beneath the editorial offices of <i>Bostonia</i>.</p> 
     <p>The literary arts magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Clarion_(journal)" title="Clarion (journal)" class="mw-redirect">Clarion</a></i> has been printed since 1998. The first issue, titled &quot;?&quot;, was published by the group Students for Literary Awareness with the sponsorship of the Department of English; subsequent issues have been issued by the BU Literary Society. <i>Burn Magazine</i> is a younger literary magazine, published biannually.</p> 
     <p>In 2006, the first issue of <i>Pusteblume</i> journal of translation was published by a group of former and current students of a co-curricular poetry seminar run by Professor George Kalogeris of the Core Curriculum. The journal, jointly sponsored by the Department of Romance Languages, the Department of Modern Languages and Comparative Literatures, and the Core Curriculum, publishes literature in translation and articles concerning translation.</p> 
     <p><i>The Journal of the Core Curriculum</i> has been published continuously since 1992 by the College of Arts and Sciences Core Curriculum. Produced by a student editorial staff with the guidance of a faculty advisor, the very interdisciplinary Core Journal publishes academic prose, literary imitations, fictitious encounters between figures from the 'great works', original poetry and creative writing, essays, artwork, translations, and even—in Vol. XVI, Spring 2007—original musical compositions. <i>The Back Bay Review</i> is a student-run journal of critical writing.</p> 
     <p><i>Arch&eacute;</i> is an annual journal of undergraduate work in philosophy, whose first issue was released in the summer of 2007. It is sponsored by the Department of Philosophy and published by the Undergraduate Philosophy Association.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_International_Relations_Review&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The International Relations Review (page does not exist)">The International Relations Review</a></i> began in 2009 as a subsidiary publication of The Boston University International Affairs Association. Entirely student-run, <i>The IR Review</i> is an independent scholarly journal publishing articles from all areas in international affairs. The goal of <i>The IRR</i> is to unite the many talents and experiences within BU's vast department of international relations.</p> 
     <p>Even more independent, <i>The Student Underground</i>, focuses on alternative political and cultural activity. Since 1997, issues have been published roughly monthly by a &quot;not-for-profit collective&quot; composed mostly of BU students. In 2007, the paper began operating under the name <i>The Boston Underground</i>; the original editorial focus on campus issues has over the years weakened as the founding editors graduated from BU or left Boston altogether.</p> 
     <p><i>The Sam Adams Review</i> was a short-lived monthly student newspaper &quot;providing news for the American Spirit,&quot; geared toward a conservative readership. Its staff was not officially recognized as a registed student activity group but, like the Underground, was entirely student-run.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Boink" title="Boink">Boink</a></i> was launched in February 2005 by a group of undergrads led by Alecia Oleyourryk, who was then a senior at the College of Communications. The magazine features BU students posing nude, as well as articles on sexuality. At the time of its first issue, the Dean of Students issued a statement explaining that &quot;the University does not endorse, nor welcome, the prospective publication Boink.&quot; The magazine was then, and remains, unaffiliated with the University.</p> 
     <p>In September 2005, the student paper <i>The Source</i> began to appear weekly, and was characterized by a predominance of arts and entertainment coverage. No new issues were printed after November 2006, and it appears the publisher Greenline Media is now defunct.</p> 
     <p>The &quot;BU Quad&quot; is an independent, student-run online magazine started in fall of 2009. The magazine features articles and columns on topics including campus news, television, food, politics, and music.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>BU Culture Shock is the official blog of the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Thurman#Honors_and_Legacy" title="Howard Thurman">Howard Thurman Center</a>, Boston University's multicultural center. It is dedicated to free expression and open discussion. Culture Shock is notable for its coverage of the 2011 Boston University Union election, inviting contributions from candidates along with other students.</p> 
     <p>Founded in spring 2009 by magazine journalism students Allie Vasilakis (COM ’11) and Marisa Morrison (COM ’11), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bubuzzmagazine.wordpress.com/">The BUZZ</a> is BU's lifestyle magazine on news and happenings on and off campus. Sections include fashion, food, music, arts and entertainment, city guide, and news. From writers to photographers, graphic designers to models, positions on the magazine's staff are all filled and run by students. The BUZZ prints one issue at the end of each academic semester and sells for $2 per issue.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_Service_Center">Community Service Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Community Service Center">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Boston University Community Service Center (CSC) is almost entirely student-run. Each semester, the CSC runs 13 volunteer programs related to issues of local, national, or global concern, including hunger, children, elders, disabilities, homelessness and affordable housing, human rights, AIDS awareness, gender issues, and the environment.</p> 
     <p>The CSC also runs two immensely popular one-week programs. During the First Year Student Outreach Project (FYSOP), upperclassmen lead groups of freshmen in volunteer activities throughout Boston before the start of first semester. For Alternative Spring Break (ASB), hundreds of students travel by 12-passenger van, bus, and airplane to locations throughout the country to do service projects in various areas of need. Before registration moved online, students camped out the day before to get spots on trips. Starting in 2010, registration process moved online.<sup id="cite_ref-bu.edu_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bu.edu-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> For the ASB 2012 program, its registration site <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dailyfreepress.com/2012/01/30/asb-registration-site-crashes-due-to-heavy-traffic-spots-filled-rapidly/">crashed</a> due to overwhelming traffic. When registration resumed later that day, spots on all trips filled within minutes, according to <i>The Daily Free Press.</i></p> 
     <p>The CSC boasts the most student involvement of any organization on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-bu.edu_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bu.edu-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_workshops">Graduate workshops</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Graduate workshops">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Willing_suspension_productions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Willing suspension productions (page does not exist)">Willing Suspension Productions</a> provides graduate English students the opportunity to present rare Early modern drama before a Boston audience. The program was founded in 1993 and produces one play per year.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ROTC">ROTC</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: ROTC">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/ROTC" title="ROTC" class="mw-redirect">Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> (ROTC) at BU traces its origins back to August 16, 1919 when the U.S. War Department stood up the Students’ Army Training Corps at Boston University, the predecessor to the current Army ROTC program.<sup id="cite_ref-rotc_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotc-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Today, BU is one of twenty five colleges and universities in the country to host all three ROTC programs – Army, Navy, and Air Force. Students wishing to be commissioned into the Marine Corps study as Navy Midshipmen.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honor_Societies">Honor Societies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Honor Societies">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Sigma" title="Alpha Phi Sigma">Alpha Phi Sigma</a> - Nu Mu Chapter</p> 
     <p>Alpha Phi Sigma, the national criminal justice honor society, recognizes academic excellence in undergraduate and graduate criminal justice students, as well as Juris Doctor (JD) students, inducting new members twice yearly. The goals of Alpha Phi Sigma are to honor and promote academic excellence, community service, and educational leadership and unity. The society was originally founded in 1942 at Washington State University. The Nu Mu chapter was chartered May 2012 at Boston University. Alpha Phi Sigma is the only criminal justice honor society certified as a member of the Association of College Honor Societies and affiliated with the Academy of Criminal Justice Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-Nu_Mu_Chapter_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nu_Mu_Chapter-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_clubs_and_activities">Other clubs and activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Other clubs and activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_Dear_Abbeys" title="Boston University Dear Abbeys" class="mw-redirect">Boston University Dear Abbeys</a> is an acclaimed All-Male student a cappella group. In 2005, they won the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_of_Collegiate_A_Cappella" title="International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella">International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella</a>, a prestigious nation-wide tournament for collegiate a cappella groups.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Boston University<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> is one of the 22 nation-wide college sites where there is a branch of <a href="/wiki/Peer_Health_Exchange" title="Peer Health Exchange">Peer Health Exchange</a>. Peer Health Exchange trains college students to become PHE Health Educators in neighboring public high schools that lack funding for health education. Health Educators teach the following topics in ninth grade classrooms: Decision-Making and Communication I, Sexual Decision-Making, Pregnancy Prevention, Sexually Transmitted Infections &amp; HIV, Healthy Relationships, Abusive Relationships, Rape &amp; Sexual Assault, Nutrition &amp; Physical Activity, Tobacco, Alcohol, Drugs, Mental Health, and Decision-Making and Communication II.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Boston_University_Stage_Troupe" title="Boston University Stage Troupe">Boston University Stage Troupe</a> is the University's oldest and largest performing arts group. Open to undergrads not majoring in theatre, the group performs many shows a year, and also hosts special events, some of which are coordinated with the Dean of Students.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <i>Boston University Debate Society</i> regularly competes on the <a href="/wiki/American_Parliamentary_Debate_Association" title="American Parliamentary Debate Association">American Parliamentary Debate Association</a> debate circuit. During the 2010–11 season, BUDS fielded debaters who won both &quot;Team of the Year&quot; distinction as well as the 2011 National Championship at West Point, NY. The team hosts an unopposed national tournament on campus each spring, with nearly every APDA college represented.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Boston University Figure Skating Club is a team of students who <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_dancing" title="Ice dancing">ice dance</a>, and a fully fledged member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Figure_Skating_Association" title="United States Figure Skating Association" class="mw-redirect">United States Figure Skating Association</a>. It is the reigning two-time U.S. National Intercollegiate Team Champion. In addition, the &quot;Boston University Terrierettes&quot; compete in Collegiate <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_skating" title="Synchronized skating">Synchronized skating</a>, and have routinely placed in the top ten at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Synchronized_Team_Skating_Championships" title="United States Synchronized Team Skating Championships" class="mw-redirect">United States Synchronized Team Skating Championships</a>.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University_International_Affairs_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boston University International Affairs Association (page does not exist)">Boston University International Affairs Association</a> (BUIAA) is the evolution of the Boston University Model United Nations Association (BUMUNA), which was founded in 1973. This club also hosts two conferences annually, one for high school students and one on the collegiate level. BosMUN,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> BUIAA's high school conference, hosts over 1,000 students annually from all across the globe. Last year, schools came from China, Guatemala, and Canada. BarMUN<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> (Boston Area Model United Nations Conference) is BUIAA's college level conference. BarMUN stands apart from other college conference in that the conference is a full scale simulation, ranging from 4 to 8 committee joint crises.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <i>Hug Don't Hate</i> grassroots peace-building campaign was founded in 2006 at Boston University with the mission of creating lasting peace through happiness, understanding and respect. All of Hug Don't Hate's activities are focused on helping individuals find common ground. The activities are divided into 4 branches: 'Free Hug Fridays', 'Urban Smiles', 'Connective Kindness' and 'BUNITED'. Hug Don't Hate is also currently expanding to different locations.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Boston University Crafts for Charity Club is an organization of students which creates crafts for local charities.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Greek community on BU's campus consists of nine sororities (nine Panhellenic chapters), ten fraternities (seven Inter-Fraternity Council chapters) and recently created Multicultural Greek Council (four fraterneties and one sorority).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Greek life on campus became shrouded in controversy in the early 2010s, with a number of high-profile incidents including hazing and a student death. Spring 2012 saw multiple hazing incidents. In March, the sorority Sigma Delta Tau was suspended by the university for alcohol-related hazing.<sup id="cite_ref-Alleged_Sorority_Hazing_Investigated_by_University.2C_Police_.28BU_Today.29_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alleged_Sorority_Hazing_Investigated_by_University.2C_Police_.28BU_Today.29-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 2012, fourteen BU students were charged with hazing, assault and battery, and failure to report hazing in connection with an alleged hazing of pledges to Alpha Epsilon Pi, a fraternity not recognized by the University.<sup id="cite_ref-Fourteen_Are_Charged_With_Hazing_.28BU_Today.29_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourteen_Are_Charged_With_Hazing_.28BU_Today.29-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2013, a male freshman died after drinking a lethal amount of alcohol at a Sigma Alpha Mu fraternity party.<sup id="cite_ref-Boston_University_student_died_from_lethal_amount_of_alcohol_.28WCVB.29_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boston_University_student_died_from_lethal_amount_of_alcohol_.28WCVB.29-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The university suspended the officially-sanctioned fraternity in response.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <i>Boston University India Club</i> is the University's largest student-run organization. Open to students of all ethnic backgrounds, the club sponsors cultural shows, performances and activities that showcase South Asian culture. BUIC also hosts and organizes the annual GarbaFest Competition, a garba raas competition.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a> (ΛΧΑ), a member of the <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">North-American Interfraternity Conference</a> (NIC) and one of the largest men's general <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a> in North America, was founded by <a href="/wiki/Warren_A._Cole" title="Warren A. Cole">Warren A. Cole</a>, while he was a student at Boston University, on November 2, 1909.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Delta Delta Delta (<a href="/wiki/Delta_Delta_Delta" title="Delta Delta Delta">ΔΔΔ</a>) was founded at Boston University on <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">Thanksgiving Eve</a>, 1888. Sarah Ida Shaw, later known as Ida Shaw Martin, founded Tri Delta without the assistance of a men's fraternity, a unique accomplishment for her time.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The College of Arts and Sciences (CAS) Dean's Hosts are a premier student volunteer organization where members serve as liaisons between CAS students and faculty members. Most notably, CAS Dean's Hosts along with CAS Student Government throw the Top of the Hub formal in downtown Boston annually.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The &quot;Boston University Soccer Club&quot; is an athletic-based club that allows members of the BU community to participate in a variety of soccer-related events ranging from pick-up <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> games at the <a href="/wiki/Fitness_and_Recreation_Center" title="Fitness and Recreation Center">Fitness and Recreation Center</a>, to philanthropic fundraising matches such as the annual &quot;Lose the Shoes&quot; charity tournament, from which all the proceeds go to the GrassrootSoccer campaign. The motto of the club is: &quot;Unifying diversity through the love of the world's beautiful game.&quot;</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>CAS Student Government is the University's largest individual student government group. Each year they work with the administration of the College of Arts and Sciences to deal with multiple student affairs issues within CAS. They also program many events for the students of CAS including: Celtics Night, Coffee at Finals, Ice Skating at Frog Pond, Senior Reception, and many more.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Boston University offers close to 500 student organizations on campus.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_Terriers" title="Boston University Terriers">Boston University Terriers</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_Terriers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Boston University Terriers men's ice hockey">Boston University Terriers men's ice hockey</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg/200px-Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg/300px-Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg/400px-Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Agganis_Arena_Exterior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Exterior of Agganis Arena.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg/200px-Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg/300px-Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg/400px-Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Inside_Agganis_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Inside 
        <a href="/wiki/Agganis_Arena" title="Agganis Arena">Agganis Arena</a> after a hockey game.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Boston University's NCAA <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> Terriers compete in men's basketball, cross country, golf, ice hockey, <a href="/wiki/Sport_rowing" title="Sport rowing" class="mw-redirect">rowing</a>, soccer, swimming, tennis, track, and <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_wrestling" title="Collegiate wrestling">wrestling</a>, and in women's basketball, dance, cross country, field hockey, golf, ice hockey, <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, rowing, soccer, softball, swimming, tennis, and track. <a href="/wiki/Boston_University_athletics" title="Boston University athletics" class="mw-redirect">Boston University athletics</a> teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_League" title="Patriot League">Patriot League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey_East" title="Hockey East">Hockey East</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Athletic_Association" title="Colonial Athletic Association">Colonial Athletic Association</a> conferences, and their mascot is Rhett the Boston Terrier. As of July 1, 2013, a majority of Boston University's teams will compete in the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_League" title="Patriot League">Patriot League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 1, 2013, the university announced it would cut its wrestling program following the 2013-14 season.</p> 
     <p>The Boston University men's hockey team is the most successful on campus, and is a storied college hockey franchise, with five NCAA championships, most recently in 2009. The team was coached by hall-of-famer Jack Parker for 40 seasons, and is a major supplier of talent to the NHL, as well as to the 1980 U.S.A. Gold Medal-winning men's hockey team. The Terriers have won 29 <a href="/wiki/Beanpot_(ice_hockey)" title="Beanpot (ice hockey)">Beanpot</a> titles, more than any other team in the tournament, which includes <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Crimson_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Harvard Crimson men's ice hockey">Harvard University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_College_Eagles_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Boston College Eagles men's ice hockey">Boston College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Huskies" title="Northeastern Huskies">Northeastern University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Boston University also won an game in 2010 against Boston College at Fenway Park by a score of 3–2, played a week after the <a href="/wiki/NHL_Winter_Classic" title="NHL Winter Classic">NHL Winter Classic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>BU has also won two national championships in women's rowing, in 1991 and 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Boston University recently constructed the new <a href="/wiki/Agganis_Arena" title="Agganis Arena">Agganis Arena</a>, which opened on January 3, 2005 with a men's hockey game between the Terriers and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a> <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">Golden Gophers</a>. The arena also hosts non-sporting events, such as concerts, ice shows, and other performances.</p> 
     <p>Boston University disbanded its football team in 1997. The university used the nearly $3 million from its football program to build the multimillion-dollar John Hancock Student Village and athletic complex. The university also increased funding to women's athletic programs. &quot;By implementing the total plan, we can achieve a much more balanced set of sports programs for both men and women, which is consistent with the philosophy underlying Title IX,&quot; said former BU athletic director Gary Strickler.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_sports">Club sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Club sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Boston University students also compete in athletics at the club level. Thirty six club sports are recognized by the university, including:<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Synchronized Skating, Baseball; Inline Hockey; Men's Volleyball; Women's Volleyball; Men's Lacrosse; Snowboard; Ultimate Frisbee; Kung Fu; Fencing; Rugby Football; Synchronized Swimming; Cheerleading; Table Tennis; Women's Water Polo; Men's Water Polo; Women's Rugby; Alpine Ski Racing; Snowboarding; Cycling; Badminton; Ballroom Dance; Figure Skating; Golf; Gymnastics; Jiu Jitsu; Kendo; Shotokan Karate; Sailing; Taekwondo; Triathlon; Dance Theater Group; Squash, Curling, Equestrian, and Men's Club Football.</p> 
     <p>The BU Dinghy Sailors are among the most prestigious sailing teams in college sailing. They have won 7 Collegiate National Championships, most recently in 1999. They have also had 3 team members graduate as &quot;College Sailor of the Year.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable alumni of the team include <a href="/wiki/Ken_Read_(sailor)" title="Ken Read (sailor)">Ken Read</a>, skipper for <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" title="Puma SE">PUMA Ocean Racing</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Ocean_Race" title="Volvo Ocean Race">Volvo Ocean Race</a>, and 2012 US Sailing Rolex Yachtsman of the Year nominee, John Mollicone.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg/220px-Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg/330px-Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg/440px-Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_River_BU_Sailing_Pavilion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> BU Sailing Pavilion.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The BU Inline Hockey Team advanced to the NCHRA Tournament in 2001, 2002, and 2003. The team advanced all the way to the Final Four in 2001.</p> 
     <p>The BU Table Tennis team has won the divisional championships a number of times this decade, most recently in 2006 (Men's) and 2007 (Women's).<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Both Men's and Women's Intervarsity Table Tennis Teams have attended the National Collegiate Table Tennis Tournaments and ranked as high as the top 10 nationwide.</p> 
     <p>The BU Figure Skating Team won the 2009 Intercollegiate National Figure Skating Championships held in Colorado Springs.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song:_.22Go_B.U..22">Fight song: &quot;Go B.U.&quot;</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Fight song: &quot;Go B.U.&quot;">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>Go BU, Go BU!<br /> Sing her praises loud and true!<br /> We'll fight for our alma mater,<br /> On to sure victory!!<br /> Fight! Fight! Fight!<br /> Go BU, Go BU!<br /> Down the field to score anew!<br /> Our hearts are with you as you meet the foe.<br /> We hail you, Ole BU!<br /></p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>The word &quot;field&quot; in the song's seventh line is replaced by &quot;ice&quot; when sung at hockey games and by &quot;court&quot; at basketball games.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boston_University_people" title="List of Boston University people">List of Boston University people</a>
     </div>

     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg/170px-Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg" width="170" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg/255px-Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg/340px-Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Luther_King_Jr_NYWTS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> earned a PhD from BU in 1955.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are 285,000 Boston University alumni, representing almost every country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> is one of BU's most notable alumni. Three other alumni hold historical importance: <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Lee_Crumpler" title="Rebecca Lee Crumpler">Rebecca Lee Crumpler</a> was the first African-American woman and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Alexander_Eastman" title="Charles Alexander Eastman" class="mw-redirect">Charles Eastman (first named Ohiyesa)</a> the first <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">American Indian</a> to be certified as doctors, and <a href="/wiki/Helen_Magill_White" title="Helen Magill White">Helen Magill White</a> was the first woman in the US to earn a PhD.</p> 
     <p>Other well-known alumni include actors <a href="/wiki/Ginnifer_Goodwin" title="Ginnifer Goodwin">Ginnifer Goodwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marisa_Tomei" title="Marisa Tomei">Marisa Tomei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emily_Deschanel" title="Emily Deschanel">Emily Deschanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julianne_Moore" title="Julianne Moore">Julianne Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geena_Davis" title="Geena Davis">Geena Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwanese</a> composer <a href="/wiki/Wen-Pin_Hope_Lee" title="Wen-Pin Hope Lee">Wen-Pin Hope Lee</a>, former Defense Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Cohen" title="William Cohen">William Cohen</a>, current U.S. Ambassador to China <a href="/wiki/Gary_Locke" title="Gary Locke">Gary Locke</a>, former Senator <a href="/wiki/Judd_Gregg" title="Judd Gregg">Judd Gregg</a>, radio personality <a href="/wiki/Howard_Stern" title="Howard Stern">Howard Stern</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Hyatt" title="Gordon Hyatt">Gordon Hyatt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> celebrity chef <a href="/wiki/Rocco_DiSpirito" title="Rocco DiSpirito">Rocco DiSpirito</a>, J.Crew CEO and former Gap Inc. CEO <a href="/wiki/Millard_Drexler" title="Millard Drexler">Millard Drexler</a>, sports writer <a href="/wiki/Bill_Simmons" title="Bill Simmons">Bill Simmons</a>, radiologist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Francois_Geschwind&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jean Francois Geschwind (page does not exist)">Jean Francois Geschwind</a>, television personality <a href="/wiki/Bill_O%27Reilly_(political_commentator)" title="Bill O'Reilly (political commentator)">Bill O'Reilly</a>, Bravo executive <a href="/wiki/Andy_Cohen_(television_personality)" title="Andy Cohen (television personality)">Andy Cohen</a>, former Second Lady <a href="/wiki/Tipper_Gore" title="Tipper Gore">Tipper Gore</a> and cohost of Project Runway and fashion editor for Marie Claire Magazine <a href="/wiki/Nina_Garcia" title="Nina Garcia">Nina Garcia</a>. The former First Vice President of the Federal Reserve Bank of Boston <a href="/wiki/Earle_O._Latham" title="Earle O. Latham">Earle O. Latham</a>. The American painter <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kline" title="Franz Kline">Franz Kline</a> attended BU. The founder of the Albanian Orthodox Church, <a href="/wiki/Fan_S._Noli" title="Fan S. Noli">Fan S. Noli</a>, received a doctorate from BU. <a href="/wiki/Infosys" title="Infosys">Infosys</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/S._D._Shibulal" title="S. D. Shibulal">S. D. Shibulal</a> did his MS from BU.<sup id="cite_ref-Avni_Spahiu_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avni_Spahiu-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> personality <a href="/wiki/Jenna_Mourey" title="Jenna Mourey" class="mw-redirect">Jenna Mourey</a> received a <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> from Boston University.</p> 
     <p>Current and former faculty of BU include <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elie_Wiesel" title="Elie Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andre_de_Quadros" title="Andre de Quadros">Andre de Quadros</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Zinn" title="Howard Zinn">Howard Zinn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Derek_Walcott" title="Derek Walcott">Derek Walcott</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Pinsky" title="Robert Pinsky">Robert Pinsky</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Zelnick" title="Bob Zelnick" class="mw-redirect">Bob Zelnick</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bacevich" title="Andrew Bacevich">Andrew Bacevich</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ha_Jin" title="Ha Jin">Ha Jin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jhumpa_Lahiri" title="Jhumpa Lahiri">Jhumpa Lahiri</a>.</p> 
     <p>A more infamous connection is with <a href="/wiki/Philip_Markoff" title="Philip Markoff">Philip Markoff</a>, the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Craiglist" title="Craiglist" class="mw-redirect">Craiglist</a> <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">Killer</a>&quot;, who was a medical student at BU.</p> 
     <p>Former <a href="/wiki/Miss_USA" title="Miss USA">Miss USA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miss_Universe" title="Miss Universe">Miss Universe</a> 2012 <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Culpo" title="Olivia Culpo">Olivia Culpo</a> attended classes at BU.</p>
